Jamison Brereton

15 (635)
Indra
Goс╣г┼лktin K─Бс╣Зv─Бyana and A┼Ыvas┼лktin K─Бс╣Зv─Бyana
13 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih, arranged in trcas, with a final verse ╠е
Attributed to the same poets as the preceding VIII.14, this hymn is a more conven tional praise hymn. It asserts the dominance of Indra over all the cosmos (esp. vss. 2тАУ6), and conversely the contribution the cosmic entities and the various other gods make to IndraтАЩs power (vss. 7тАУ10). The final tr╠еca (10тАУ12), with its coda apparently addressed to Soma (vs. 13), seeks to harness all IndraтАЩs powers for victory for our side, and thus echoes the poetтАЩs opening charge to his comrades (vs. 1). The return to the beginning is also signaled by a ring-compositional device: the first two p─Бdas of verse 11 are almost identical to those of verse 3 in the Sanskrit, though their translations diverge somewhat.
Both the language and the structure of this hymn are straightforward, but its relatively simplicity avoids the banal by the deft balancing of the powers in the two contrastive sections of the hymn and the unembellished grandeur of the rhetoric.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

English translation:

тАЬGlorify him the invoked of many, the praised of many; adore the powerful Indra with hymns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sing forth to him, much invoked and much praised.
Seek to entice mighty Indra here with hymns,

Griffith

SING forth to him whom many men invoke, to him whom many laud.
Invite the powerful Indra with your songs of praise.

Geldner

Auf ihn stimmet den Gesang an, auf den Vielgerufenen, Vielbesungenen! Den starken Indra bittet mit Lobreden her!

Grassmann

Wohlan, den vielgepriesenen, den vielgerufenen besingt; Den starken Indra, mit Gesang gewinnt ihn euch,

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe vast strength of whom, powerful in both (regions), has sustained the heaven and earth, and by itsvigour (upheld) the swift clouds and flowing waters.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Swift clouds: gir─лn ajr─Бn = quick mountains, i.e. beforetheir wings are clipped

Jamison Brereton

Him, the doubly lofty, whose lofty power holds fast the two
world-halves,
the mountains and plains, the waters and sun, through his bullishness.

Griffith

Whose lofty might-for doubly strong is he-supports the heavens and earth,
And hills and plains and floods and light with manly power.

Geldner

Des doppelstarken hohe Macht beide Welten erh├дlt, die Berge, die Ebenen, die Gew├дsser, die Sonne durch seine Bullenkraft.

Grassmann

Den zwiefach starken, dessen Macht gewaltig Erd’ und Himmel h├дlt, Gebirge, Fluren, Wasser, Licht mit Manneskraft.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, the praised of many, reign; you, single, have slain many enemies, in order to acquire the spoils ofvictory and abundant food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, o much praised one, are the ruler; you alone keep smashing obstacles,
o Indra, to extend victories and (deeds) worthy of fame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

By the rules established in Jamison 1992 for s├б with 2nd ps. reference, s├б r─Бjasi here is in violation. But notice that this line (s├б r─Бjasi puruс╣гс╣нutam╠Р, ├йko vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бс╣Зi jighnase) is twinned with 11ab satr─Б╠Бtv├бm puruс╣гс╣нutam╠Р, ├йko vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бс╣Зi to┼Ыase, which begins with satr─Б╠Б, phonologically like our s├б r─Б … Also note v├н r─Бjasi in 5c, which could invoke a *s├бс╣Г r─Бjasi here (which would change the meter, but not improperly).

For s├бm тИЪr─Бj / v├н тИЪr─Бj, see I.188.5 vir─Б╠Бс╣н samr─Б╠Бс╣н … And note that samr─Б╠Бjam is the second word of the next hymn (VIII.16.1).

To gain, O Indra, spoils of war and high renown.

English translation:

тАЬWe celebrate, thunderer, your exhilaration, the showerer (of benefits), the overcomer (of foes) in battle,the maker of the world, the glorious with your steeds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Lokakс╣Ыtnu = the provider of a plural ce (for his worshipper),sth─Бnasya kart─Бram;

Hari┼Ыriyam = him who is to be served by his steeds, a┼Ыvabhyam sevyam

Jamison Brereton

We hymn your exhilaration, an overpowering bull in battles,
creating wide space, bringing the splendor of fallow bays, o master of the stoneтАФ

Griffith

We sing this strong and wild delight of thine which conquers in the fray,
Which, Caster of the Stone! gives room and shines like gold.

By which you found the lights for ─Аyu and Manu.

Now joying in this sacred grass thou beamest forth.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрдВ рддрддреН рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рдмрд▓рдореН рдЕрджреНрдп рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЕрджреНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдХрд╛рд▓ рдЗрд╡ рдЙрдХреНрдерд┐рдирдГ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдгрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рдЕрдиреБ рд╖реНрдЯреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реГрд╖рдкрддреНрдиреАрдГ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рдкрд░реНрдЬрдиреНрдпрдГ рдкрддрд┐рд░реНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢реАрдГ рдЕрдкрдГ рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рдВ рдЬрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдпрддреНрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe reciters of prayer celebrate that your (exhilaration) now as of old; do you daily hold in subjectionthe waters, the wives of the showerer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even today do the reciters praise this (deed) of yours, as in the earlier way: you shall win the waters, whose husband is a bull, day after day.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In c jay─Б can be a 2nd sg. imperative with lengthened final (so Pp., Grassmann, Geldner) or a subjunctive (jay─Бс╕е out of sandhi). Although an undoubted form of the imperative is found in 12c (jaya), I weakly favor the subjunctive here, the idea being that the praisers keep praising the same deed, and so he will keep doing it.

Griffith

This day too singers of the hymn praise, as of old, this might of thine:
Win thou the waters day by day, thralls of the strong.

Geldner

Dies singen dir immer wieder noch heute die Liederdichter wie fr├╝her: Erobere Tag f├╝r Tag die Gew├дsser, die dem Bullen verm├дhlt sind.

Grassmann

Das r├╝hmen deine S├дnger hier auch heute wie in alter Zeit, Erk├дmpf die Stier-beherrschte Flut an jedem Tag.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдмреГрд╣рдиреН рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рдХреНрд╖рдпрдГ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рд╣реЗрддреБрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреБрдГ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ рдЪ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдЧреГрдгрд╛рддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рдорд░реБрддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╢рд░реНрдзрдГ рдмрд▓рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреБ рдорджрддрд┐ рддрд╡ рдорджрдордиреБрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рдиреНрдорд╛рджреНрдпрддрд┐ ред рддреНрд╡рд╛рдордиреБрдорд╛рджрдпрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬViс╣гс╣Зu, the mighty giver of dwellings, praises you, and Mitra and Varuс╣Зa; the company of the Marutsimitates you in exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Viс╣гс╣Зu, the lofty dwelling place, hymns you, as do Mitra and Varuс╣Зa. The Marut troop cheers you on.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since kс╣г├бya- otherwise means only тАШdwelling placeтАЩ, the text as we have it means тАЬViс╣гс╣Зu, the lofty dwelling place,тАЭ as in the published translation, not тАЬder hohe WohnerтАЭ (my italics), as Geldner would have it. Already BR (see Grassmann s.v. kс╣г├бya-) suggested that we read instead a bahuvr─лhi *bс╣Ыh├бt-kс╣гayaс╕е тАШhaving a lofty dwelling placeтАЩ. This of course makes better immediate sense, but I think we can keep the text as we have it and also avoid making kс╣г├бya- into a nonce agent noun (per Geldner). Given the flexibility of RVic diction, it is not difficult to identify a god with his most characteristic product тАФin this case, Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs three footsteps, particularly his highest one, which becomes an important locus in heaven (see, e.g., I.22.19-21) тАФ and he elsewhere is said to create dwelling places: VII.100.4 v├н cakrame pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бm eс╣г├б et─Б╠Бс╣Г, kс╣г├йtr─Бya v├нс╣гс╣Зur m─Б╠Бnuс╣гe тАж / urukс╣гit├нm тАж cak─Бra тАЬQuick Viс╣гс╣Зu strode across this earth for a dwelling place for Manu тАж / He has made wide dwelling.тАЭ In the RVic conceptual realm it is just one step from creating a dwelling place to being a dwelling place. The identification of Soma with a dwelling place in vs. 13 below supports the literal reading here.

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra), the praised of many, you alone destroy many mighty foes; no other Indra achieves such greatexploits.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In every way, o much-praised one, you alone stream over obstacles. None other than Indra spurs more action.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this verse forming a ring with 3ab, see introduction. and comments on vs. 3.

Griffith

Ever, alone, O highly-praised, thou sendest Vrtras to their rest:
None else than Indra executes the mighty deed.

Geldner

Du Vielbesungener sprengst allein die Feinde allzumal in die Flucht; keiner als Indra bringt dieses Werk zustande.

Grassmann

Du legst allein, gepriesener, die Feinde allesammt zur Ruh; Kein andrer f├╢rdert mehr das Werk, als Indra du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen (in the combat), Indra, they invoke you in many ways with praise for protection, then do you (soinvoked) by our leaders overcome all (our enemies).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When, o Indra, they call upon you for help, every man for himself, according to his own thought,
with our superior men win the sun now.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note that n─Б╠Бn─Б opening b picks up n─Б╠Бny├б(с╕е) opening vs. 11.

Griffith

Though here and there, in varied hymns, Indra, men call on thee for aid,
Still with our heroes fight and win the light of heaven.

Geldner

Wenn sie dich, Indra, von verschiedenen Seiten je nach ihren Absichten zu Hilfe rufen, so gewinne du dabei mit unseren Herren das Sonnenlicht!

Grassmann

Wenn, Indra, auch nach ihrem Sinn um Huld dich viele rufen an, So m├╢gst du Glanz gewinnen doch durch unsre Schar.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAll the forms (of Indra) have sufficiently entered into our own spacious abode; gratify Indra the lord of┼Ъac─л, (that he may give us) the spoil of victory.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

All the forms: i.e. the various attributes celebrated in ourpraises

Jamison Brereton

Fit (to be) a great dwelling for us, entering into all forms, (o Soma,) excite Indra, the lord of power, to victory.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The identity of the addressee in this verse is not overt. As Geldner points out, S─Бyaс╣Зa suggests that the singer is addressing himself, though p─Бdas ab make difficulties for that interpretation. Oldenberg argues for Soma, which seems likely even though, unusually for an Indra hymn, soma has not previously figured in this hymn. However, all three p─Бdas have parallels in the soma maс╣Зс╕Нala: for p─Бda a see IX.109.3c mah├й kс╣г├бy─Бya; p─Бda b is repeated in IX.25.4a modifying soma; and IX.111.3e is identical to the first three words in p─Бda c, save for the grammatical identity of the verb form (3rd pl. injunctive in IX.111.3, 2nd sg. imperative here). That Soma is the addressee here and so the subject of the impv. harс╣гay─Б is also supported by vs. 4 in the next hymn (VIII.16), where the exhilarating drinks (of soma) are called harс╣гum├бnt-.

Again, as in vs. 9, Geldner waters down the meaning of kс╣г├бya- to fit the context (тАЬdweller,тАЭ not тАЬdwellingтАЭ), but in his n. suggests that the dwelling, namely heaven, stands as a metonym for its inhabitants, the gods. I prefer not to recast and paraphrase the literal sense as Geldner does, especially since, as it stands, this half-verse expresses a small but neat paradox involving container/contained: Soma both enters everything (b) and provides a vessel in which everything (or “we” anyway) can dwell (a).

In c ja├нtr─Бya picks up ja├нtr─Б in 3c.

Griffith

Already have all forms of him entered our spacious dwelling-place:
For victory stir thou Indra, up, the Lord of Might.

Geldner

Sei uns f├╝r den gro├Яen Wohner bereit, alle Formen annehmend, mache dem Indra, dem Herrn der Kraft, Lust zum Siege!

Grassmann

Zum Heile f├╝r unsern grossen Wohnsitz dich in alle Gestalten kleidend, begeistere den Indra, den Herrn der Kraft, zum Siege.

Elizarenkova
